```

# big-code-k8s-bug-001: Missing ResourceSlice Event Handler in Kubernetes Scheduler

## Task

Investigate a bug in the Kubernetes scheduler where pods requesting Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA) devices become permanently stuck in an Unschedulable state when the DRA driver starts after the pod is created. Trace the execution path through the scheduler's event-driven re-queuing architecture to identify why ResourceSlice creation/update events are silently dropped.

## Context

- **Repository**: github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.30.0 (mirror of kubernetes/kubernetes) (Go, ~3.5M LOC)
- **Category**: Bug Investigation
- **Difficulty**: hard
- **Entry Point**: `pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go` — `ScheduleOne()` method

## Symptom

When a pod requests a DRA device and the DRA driver starts *after* the pod is created, the pod becomes permanently stuck in `Pending` with reason `Unschedulable`. The scheduler logs `"cannot allocate all claims"` because no ResourceSlices exist at scheduling time. After the driver starts and publishes ResourceSlice objects, the pod should be rescheduled — but it never is.

The bug is a race condition: if the driver starts first, scheduling succeeds immediately. But if the pod arrives before the driver, the scheduler never retries because ResourceSlice events are not wired into the scheduling queue's re-evaluation mechanism.

## Requirements

1. Starting from the entry point, trace the execution path to the root cause
2. Identify the specific file(s) and line(s) where the bug originates
3. Explain WHY the bug occurs — focus on the event handler registration mechanism and the scheduling queue's re-evaluation trigger
4. Propose a fix with specific code changes

## Expected Output

292026-03-11T17:51:36.069896agentmessage-
I am thinking...: Now I can clearly see the bug. In the `EventsToRegister()` function of the `dynamicResources` plugin (lines 381-413), the plugin registers for these events:
1. ResourceClaimParameters (Add | Update)
2. ResourceClassParameters (Add | Update)
3. ResourceClaim (Add | Update)
4. PodSchedulingContext (Add | Update)
5. Node (Add | UpdateNodeLabel | UpdateNodeTaint)
6. ResourceClass (Add | Update)

**Notably missing**: `ResourceSlice` (Add | Update)

With structured parameters (the new DRA mode in k8s v1.30), drivers advertise available devices by creating/updating `ResourceSlice` objects. When a pod is unschedulable because no ResourceSlices exist (the driver hasn't started yet), the scheduler puts the pod in the unschedulable queue.

But when the driver later starts and creates ResourceSlice objects, the scheduler never gets notified to re-try scheduling the pod because:
1. `ResourceSlice` GVK is not defined in `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` (no constant defined)
2. The `dynamicResources` plugin's `EventsToRegister()` doesn't register for ResourceSlice add/update events
3. Even if the plugin tried to register for ResourceSlice events, there's no case in `addAllEventHandlers()` for ResourceSlice, so no informer handler would be set up

So there are two bugs:
1. Missing `ResourceSlice` GVK constant in `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`
2. Missing `ResourceSlice` event in `dynamicResources.EventsToRegister()`
3. Missing case for `ResourceSlice` in `addAllEventHandlers()` in `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go`

Wait, let me re-examine. The flow is:
1. Plugin registers events via `EventsToRegister()`
2. The scheduler's `addAllEventHandlers()` sets up informer callbacks that call `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` with those events
3. The queue only moves pods if

352026-03-11T17:52:22.525546agentmessage-
I am thinking...: Now I understand the complete picture. Let me trace the full chain:

1. `Scheduler.New()` in `scheduler.go:359` calls `addAllEventHandlers(sched, informerFactory, dynInformerFactory, unionedGVKs(queueingHintsPerProfile))`

2. `unionedGVKs()` collects all events registered by plugins via `EventsToRegister()`. The `dynamicResources` plugin registers these events (line 386-411 in dynamicresources.go):
   - ResourceClaimParameters (Add | Update)
   - ResourceClassParameters (Add | Update)
   - ResourceClaim (Add | Update)
   - PodSchedulingContext (Add | Update)
   - Node (Add | UpdateNodeLabel | UpdateNodeTaint)
   - ResourceClass (Add | Update)
   
   **NOT** ResourceSlice!

3. `addAllEventHandlers()` takes the gvkMap and creates informer event handlers. For each GVK in the map, it calls `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` when objects of that type are created/updated/deleted.

4. Since `ResourceSlice` is not in `EventsToRegister()`, and thus not in `gvkMap`, no informer handler for ResourceSlice is ever created.

5. When the DRA driver starts and publishes ResourceSlice objects, the informer notices the objects but there are no registered handlers for ResourceSlice - so the queue is never notified to retry the unschedulable pod.

**The root cause**: The `dynamicResources` plugin's `EventsToRegister()` function doesn't include `ResourceSlice` events. Additionally, there's no `ResourceSlice` GVK constant defined in `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`.

**Two-part fix needed**:
1. Add `ResourceSlice GVK = "ResourceSlice"` constant to `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`
2. Add `{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceSlice, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}}` to `EventsToRegister()` in `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresou

502026-03-11T17:53:53.503417agentmessage-
I am thinking...: Now I have a very complete picture of the bug. Let me trace the key code path:

1. In `PreFilter()` (line 958), when `needResourceInformation` is true (meaning a claim uses structured parameters), it calls `newResourceModel()` which lists all ResourceSlices to understand available resources. If no ResourceSlices exist (driver not started), the model will be empty.

2. In `Filter()` (line 1138-1148), for claims using structured parameters, it calls `state.informationsForClaim[index].controller.nodeIsSuitable(ctx, node.Name, state.resources)`. If `state.resources` is empty (no ResourceSlices), `nodeIsSuitable` returns false, so the node is filtered out and the pod is marked unschedulable.

3. Then in `schedulingCycle()` back in `schedule_one.go`, a FitError is returned.

4. Back in `ScheduleOne()`, `sched.FailureHandler()` is called, which eventually calls `handleSchedulingFailure()`. This will put the pod into the unschedulable queue.

5. The pod stays there waiting for a relevant cluster event to trigger re-queuing.

**The bug**: The `EventsToRegister()` function in `dynamicresources.go` (line 381-413) doesn't include `ResourceSlice` events. So when the DRA driver starts and publishes ResourceSlice objects, no handler is registered to call `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` with a ResourceSlice event. The pod remains stuck in the unschedulable queue forever.

**Additionally**, even if `EventsToRegister()` registered for a `ResourceSlice` GVK, the `addAllEventHandlers()` function in `eventhandlers.go` (lines 395-542) doesn't have a case for `ResourceSlice`. Looking at the switch cases:
- The specific known GVKs are handled by named cases
- The `default` case handles unknown GVKs via dynamic informers, but requires the GVK string to be in a specific forma
... (truncated)

572026-03-11T17:56:03.966637agentmessage-
The analysis is complete. Here is a summary of the full investigation:

---

## Bug Summary: DRA Pods Permanently Stuck Unschedulable

### Root Cause

The bug is a **missing event registration** — three coordinated defects that together silence `ResourceSlice` creation events from ever reaching the pod re-queuing logic.

---

### The Full Causal Chain

#### Step 1 — ScheduleOne kicks off the cycle (`pkg/scheduler/schedule_one.go`)
`ScheduleOne()` dequeues the pod, calls `schedulingCycle()` → `SchedulePod()` → runs all Filter plugins.

#### Step 2 — DynamicResources PreFilter builds an empty resource model
`PreFilter()` (line ~958) calls `newResourceModel(logger, pl.resourceSliceLister, ...)`. `newResourceModel()` calls `resourceSliceLister.List(labels.Everything())`. **No ResourceSlices exist yet** (driver not started), so `state.resources` is an empty map.

#### Step 3 — DynamicResources Filter rejects every node
`Filter()` (line ~1138–1148) calls `controller.nodeIsSuitable(ctx, node.Name, state.resources)` for each structured-parameter claim. The empty resource map means the check returns `false` for all nodes → `statusUnschedulable("resourceclaim cannot be allocated for the node (unsuitable)")`.

#### Step 4 — Pod lands in the unschedulable pool
`ScheduleOne()` calls `sched.FailureHandler()` → `handleSchedulingFailure()`. The pod is moved to the **unschedulable pod pool**, tagged with `DynamicResources` as the rejecting plugin.

#### Step 5 — Re-queue requires a registered cluster event
The scheduling queue (`pkg/scheduler/internal/queue`) moves pods from unschedulable back to `activeQ` only when a matching cluster event fires. The mapping is built in `scheduler.go:buildQueueingHintMap()` from each plugin's `EventsToRegister()`.

#### Step 6 — ResourceSlice is missin

ResourceClaimParameters (Add | Update)\n2. ResourceClassParameters (Add | Update)\n3. ResourceClaim (Add | Update)\n4. PodSchedulingContext (Add | Update)\n5. Node (Add | UpdateNodeLabel | UpdateNodeTaint)\n6. ResourceClass (Add | Update)\n\n**Notably missing**: `ResourceSlice` (Add | Update)\n\nWith structured parameters (the new DRA mode in k8s v1.30), drivers advertise available devices by creating/updating `ResourceSlice` objects. When a pod is unschedulable because no ResourceSlices exist (the driver hasn't started yet), the scheduler puts the pod in the unschedulable queue.\n\nBut when the driver later starts and creates ResourceSlice objects, the scheduler never gets notified to re-try scheduling the pod because:\n1. `ResourceSlice` GVK is not defined in `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` (no constant defined)\n2. The `dynamicResources` plugin's `EventsToRegister()` doesn't register for ResourceSlice add/update events\n3. Even if the plugin tried to register for ResourceSlice events, there's no case in `addAllEventHandlers()` for ResourceSlice, so no informer handler would be set up\n\nSo there are two bugs:\n1. Missing `ResourceSlice` GVK constant in `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`\n2. Missing `ResourceSlice` event in `dynamicResources.EventsToRegister()`\n3. Missing case for `ResourceSlice` in `addAllEventHandlers()` in `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go`\n\nWait, let me re-examine. The flow is:\n1. Plugin registers events via `EventsToRegister()`\n2. The scheduler's `addAllEventHandlers()` sets up informer callbacks that call `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` with those events\n3. The queue only moves pods if a registered event matches\n\nActually wait - looking more carefully at `addAllEventHandlers()`, the `gvkMap` parameter is built from the registered plugins' `EventsToRegister()`. If the plugin doesn't register for `ResourceSlice`, then `gvkMap` won't have `ResourceSlice`, so the `for gvk, at := range gvkMap` loop won't create a handler for `ResourceSlice`.\n\nBut there's more - the `switch gvk` block only handles specific known GVKs. If `ResourceSlice` were in `gvkMap` (via plugin registration), it would fall into the `default` case which uses dynamic informers. But since the plugin doesn't register it, and there's no GVK constant for it, the whole chain is broken.\n\nLet me look at how `gvkMap` is built to understand the full picture.\n"

Let me trace the full chain:\n\n1. `Scheduler.New()` in `scheduler.go:359` calls `addAllEventHandlers(sched, informerFactory, dynInformerFactory, unionedGVKs(queueingHintsPerProfile))`\n\n2. `unionedGVKs()` collects all events registered by plugins via `EventsToRegister()`. The `dynamicResources` plugin registers these events (line 386-411 in dynamicresources.go):\n   - ResourceClaimParameters (Add | Update)\n   - ResourceClassParameters (Add | Update)\n   - ResourceClaim (Add | Update)\n   - PodSchedulingContext (Add | Update)\n   - Node (Add | UpdateNodeLabel | UpdateNodeTaint)\n   - ResourceClass (Add | Update)\n   \n   **NOT** ResourceSlice!\n\n3. `addAllEventHandlers()` takes the gvkMap and creates informer event handlers. For each GVK in the map, it calls `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` when objects of that type are created/updated/deleted.\n\n4. Since `ResourceSlice` is not in `EventsToRegister()`, and thus not in `gvkMap`, no informer handler for ResourceSlice is ever created.\n\n5. When the DRA driver starts and publishes ResourceSlice objects, the informer notices the objects but there are no registered handlers for ResourceSlice - so the queue is never notified to retry the unschedulable pod.\n\n**The root cause**: The `dynamicResources` plugin's `EventsToRegister()` function doesn't include `ResourceSlice` events. Additionally, there's no `ResourceSlice` GVK constant defined in `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`.\n\n**Two-part fix needed**:\n1. Add `ResourceSlice GVK = \"ResourceSlice\"` constant to `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`\n2. Add `{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceSlice, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}}` to `EventsToRegister()` in `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n3. Add a case for `framework.ResourceSlice` in `addAllEventHandlers()` in `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go`\n\nWait, let me reconsider point 3. Looking at `addAllEventHandlers()`, the `switch gvk` handles specific known GVKs. But wait - if `ResourceSlice` is not in the switch, and it's not a `Node` or `Pod` (which are excluded), then it would fall to the `default` case which uses the dynamic informer factory. The dynamic informer factory can handle any GVK.\n\nHowever, I need to check whether `addAllEventHandlers()` needs a specific case for ResourceSlice, or whether the default case with dynInformerFactory can handle it.\n\nLooking at the default case:\n```go\ndefault:\n    if dynInformerFactory == nil {\n        continue\n    }\n    // GVK is expected to be at least 3-folded, separated by dots.\n    // <kind in plural>.<version>.<group>\n    if strings.Count(string(gvk), \".\") < 2 {\n        logger.Error(nil, \"incorrect event registration\", \"gvk\", gvk)\n        continue\n    }\n    // Fall back to try dynamic informers.\n    gvr, _ := schema.ParseResourceArg(string(gvk))\n    dynInformer := dynInformerFactory.ForResource(*gvr).Informer()\n    ...\n```\n\nThe default case requires the GVK string to be in the format `<kind in plural>.<version>.<group>` with at least 3 sections separated by dots. But if we define `ResourceSlice GVK = \"ResourceSlice\"` (similar to other constants like `ResourceClaim GVK = \"ResourceClaim\"`), it would NOT have 2 dots, so the default case would log an error and skip it.\n\nSo we need a specific case in the switch for `ResourceSlice` similar to what we have for `ResourceClaim`, `ResourceClass`, etc. That specific case would use the typed informer `informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceSlices().Informer()`.\n\nLet me also look at the structuredparameters.go to understand how ResourceSlice is used in the DRA scheduling logic.\n"

  "thought": "Now I have a very complete picture of the bug. Let me trace the key code path:\n\n1. In `PreFilter()` (line 958), when `needResourceInformation` is true (meaning a claim uses structured parameters), it calls `newResourceModel()` which lists all ResourceSlices to understand available resources. If no ResourceSlices exist (driver not started), the model will be empty.\n\n2. In `Filter()` (line 1138-1148), for claims using structured parameters, it calls `state.informationsForClaim[index].controller.nodeIsSuitable(ctx, node.Name, state.resources)`. If `state.resources` is empty (no ResourceSlices), `nodeIsSuitable` returns false, so the node is filtered out and the pod is marked unschedulable.\n\n3. Then in `schedulingCycle()` back in `schedule_one.go`, a FitError is returned.\n\n4. Back in `ScheduleOne()`, `sched.FailureHandler()` is called, which eventually calls `handleSchedulingFailure()`. This will put the pod into the unschedulable queue.\n\n5. The pod stays there waiting for a relevant cluster event to trigger re-queuing.\n\n**The bug**: The `EventsToRegister()` function in `dynamicresources.go` (line 381-413) doesn't include `ResourceSlice` events. So when the DRA driver starts and publishes ResourceSlice objects, no handler is registered to call `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` with a ResourceSlice event. The pod remains stuck in the unschedulable queue forever.\n\n**Additionally**, even if `EventsToRegister()` registered for a `ResourceSlice` GVK, the `addAllEventHandlers()` function in `eventhandlers.go` (lines 395-542) doesn't have a case for `ResourceSlice`. Looking at the switch cases:\n- The specific known GVKs are handled by named cases\n- The `default` case handles unknown GVKs via dynamic informers, but requires the GVK string to be in a specific format (with dots as separators)\n- `ResourceSlice` as a simple string wouldn't have dots, so it would fail the dot-count check and be silently skipped\n\n**The complete fix requires three changes**:\n\n1. **`pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`**: Add `ResourceSlice GVK = \"ResourceSlice\"` constant.\n\n2. **`pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`**: Add ResourceSlice to `EventsToRegister()`:\n   ```go\n   {Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceSlice, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}},\n   ```\n\n3. **`pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go`**: Add a case for `ResourceSlice` in the `switch gvk` block:\n   ```go\n   case framework.ResourceSlice:\n       if utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n           if handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceSlices().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n               buildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceSlice, \"ResourceSlice\"),\n           ); err != nil {\n               return err\n           }\n           handlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n       }\n   ```\n\nThe **primary root cause** is in `EventsToRegister()` in `dynamicresources.go`. Without registering for ResourceSlice events, the scheduler has no way to know that new ResourceSlices have been published by the driver, and can never re-evaluate the stuck pod.\n\nHowever, the fix also requires the GVK constant in `types.go` and the informer handler in `eventhandlers.go` to make the whole chain work.\n\nLet me now also check what exact error message is logged when structured parameters can't allocate resources.\n"

When the driver later starts and publishes `ResourceSlice` objects, no handler is wired to call `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` for that event.\n\n6. **No informer handler registered for ResourceSlice**: `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` \u2014 `addAllEventHandlers()` (line ~395-542) iterates over `gvkMap` (built from `EventsToRegister()` results). Even if it were registered by the plugin, the `switch gvk` block has no `case framework.ResourceSlice:` arm; the default arm would require the GVK string to have 2+ dots (for dynamic informers), which `\"ResourceSlice\"` does not satisfy.\n\n7. **Bug triggered by**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` \u2014 `EventsToRegister()` at line ~386-411.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n- **File**: `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n- **Function**: `EventsToRegister()`\n- **Line**: ~386\u2013411\n- **Explanation**: The `dynamicResources` scheduling plugin uses `ResourceSlice` objects (published by DRA drivers) to build an availability model for structured-parameter DRA claims. When a pod's claim cannot be allocated because no `ResourceSlice` exists, the pod is placed in the unschedulable queue. The scheduler's re-queuing mechanism works by matching future cluster events against events registered by each plugin via `EventsToRegister()`. Because `EventsToRegister()` does not include a `{Resource: framework.ResourceSlice, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}` entry, the scheduler is never instructed to retry the pod when a DRA driver later creates or updates `ResourceSlice` objects. The pod is permanently stuck.\n\n  Two supporting defects make a complete fix necessary:\n  1. `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` has no `ResourceSlice` GVK constant \u2014 needed for the plugin to reference the type.\n  2. `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go`'s `addAllEventHandlers()` switch has no `case framework.ResourceSlice:` arm to wire up the typed informer \u2014 needed so the informer callback actually calls `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` when `ResourceSlice` objects arrive.\n\n## Proposed Fix\n\n### 1. Add `ResourceSlice` GVK constant \u2014 `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`\n\n```diff\n \tResourceClaimParameters GVK = \"ResourceClaimParameters\"\n \tResourceClassParameters GVK = \"ResourceClassParameters\"\n+\tResourceSlice           GVK = \"ResourceSlice\"\n\n \t// WildCard is a special GVK to match all resources.\n```\n\n### 2. Register `ResourceSlice` events in the plugin \u2014 `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`\n\n```diff\n \tevents := []framework.ClusterEventWithHint{\n \t\t// Changes for claim or class parameters creation may make pods\n \t\t// schedulable which depend on claims using those parameters.\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClaimParameters, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClaimParametersChange},\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClassParameters, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClassParametersChange},\n\n \t\t// Allocation is tracked in ResourceClaims, so any changes may make the pods schedulable.\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClaim, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterClaimChange},\n \t\t// When a driver has provided additional information, a pod waiting for that information\n \t\t// may be schedulable.\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.PodSchedulingContext, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}, QueueingHintFn: pl.isSchedulableAfterPodSchedulingContextChange},\n \t\t// A resource might depend on node labels for topology filtering.\n \t\t// A new or updated node may make pods schedulable.\n \t\t//\n \t\t// A note about UpdateNodeTaint event:\n \t\t// NodeAdd QueueingHint isn't always called because of the internal feature called preCheck.\n \t\t// As a common problematic scenario,\n \t\t// when a node is added but not ready, NodeAdd event is filtered out by preCheck and doesn't arrive.\n \t\t// In such cases, this plugin may miss some events that actually make pods schedulable.\n \t\t// As a workaround, we add UpdateNodeTaint event to catch the case.\n \t\t// We can remove UpdateNodeTaint when we remove the preCheck feature.\n \t\t// See: https://github.com/kubernetes/kubernetes/issues/110175\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.Node, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.UpdateNodeLabel | framework.UpdateNodeTaint}},\n \t\t// A pod might be waiting for a class to get created or modified.\n \t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceClass, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}},\n+\t\t// A ResourceSlice stores the devices available on a node for structured-parameter\n+\t\t// DRA drivers. When a driver starts and publishes ResourceSlices, pods waiting for\n+\t\t// those devices must be re-evaluated.\n+\t\t{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceSlice, ActionType: framework.Add | framework.Update}},\n \t}\n \treturn events\n```\n\n### 3. Wire up the ResourceSlice informer \u2014 `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go`\n\n```diff\n \t\tcase framework.ResourceClassParameters:\n \t\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n \t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceClassParameters().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n \t\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceClassParameters, \"ResourceClassParameters\"),\n \t\t\t\t); err != nil {\n \t\t\t\t\treturn err\n \t\t\t\t}\n \t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n \t\t\t}\n+\t\tcase framework.ResourceSlice:\n+\t\t\tif utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.DynamicResourceAllocation) {\n+\t\t\t\tif handlerRegistration, err = informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceSlices().Informer().AddEventHandler(\n+\t\t\t\t\tbuildEvtResHandler(at, framework.ResourceSlice, \"ResourceSlice\"),\n+\t\t\t\t); err != nil {\n+\t\t\t\t\treturn err\n+\t\t\t\t}\n+\t\t\t\thandlers = append(handlers, handlerRegistration)\n+\t\t\t}\n \t\tcase framework.StorageClass:\n```\n\n## Analysis\n\n### Step 1 \u2014 Scheduling attempt (ScheduleOne)\n\n`ScheduleOne()` dequeues a pod and calls `schedulingCycle()` \u2192 `SchedulePod()` \u2192 runs all Filter plugins in parallel. The `DynamicResources` plugin is one of them.\n\n### Step 2 \u2014 DynamicResources PreFilter builds an empty resource model\n\nIn `PreFilter()` (line 948\u2013964), when a claim uses structured parameters (`class.StructuredParameters == true`), the plugin calls:\n\n```go\nresources, err := newResourceModel(logger, pl.resourceSliceLister, pl.claimAssumeCache, &pl.inFlightAllocations)\n```\n\n`newResourceModel()` in `structuredparameters.go` (line 51) does:\n\n```go\nslices, err := resourceSliceLister.List(labels.Everything())\n```\n\nIf the DRA driver has not yet started, there are zero `ResourceSlice` objects, so `resources` is an empty map.\n\n### Step 3 \u2014 DynamicResources Filter rejects every node\n\nIn `Filter()` (line 1138\u20131148), for each unallocated claim using structured parameters:\n\n```go\nsuitable, err := state.informationsForClaim[index].controller.nodeIsSuitable(ctx, node.Name, state.resources)\n```\n\n`state.resources` is empty (no ResourceSlices), so `nodeIsSuitable` returns `false` for every node. The plugin returns `Unschedulable` for all nodes, producing a `FitError`.\n\n### Step 4 \u2014 Pod lands in the unschedulable queue\n\nBack in `schedulingCycle()` (`schedule_one.go` line 159\u2013189), the `FitError` causes an `Unschedulable` status to be returned. `ScheduleOne()` at line 112\u2013114 calls `sched.FailureHandler()` \u2192 `handleSchedulingFailure()`, which enqueues the pod into the **unschedulable pod pool** of `SchedulingQueue`, labelled with `DynamicResources` as the rejecting plugin.\n\n### Step 5 \u2014 The scheduling queue's re-evaluation mechanism\n\nThe scheduling queue moves pods from the unschedulable pool to `activeQ` or `backoffQ` only when a matching **cluster event** fires. The mapping from \"which event re-queues which pod\" is maintained in `queueingHintsPerProfile`, built in `scheduler.go:buildQueueingHintMap()` by iterating over each plugin's `EventsToRegister()` list (lines 374\u2013410).\n\nFor a pod rejected by `DynamicResources`, the queue will call `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` only for cluster events that `DynamicResources` registered.\n\n### Step 6 \u2014 ResourceSlice events are not registered\n\n`dynamicResources.EventsToRegister()` (lines 386\u2013411) registers for:\n- `ResourceClaimParameters` Add/Update\n- `ResourceClassParameters` Add/Update\n- `ResourceClaim` Add/Update\n- `PodSchedulingContext` Add/Update\n- `Node` Add/UpdateNodeLabel/UpdateNodeTaint\n- `ResourceClass` Add/Update\n\n**`ResourceSlice` is conspicuously absent.**\n\nWhen the DRA driver starts and creates `ResourceSlice` objects, the `ResourceSlice` informer fires, but because `ResourceSlice` is not in `EventsToRegister()`, it is not in `gvkMap`, so `addAllEventHandlers()` never registers a callback for it. No `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` call is ever made for a `ResourceSlice` event.\n\n### Step 7 \u2014 Double absence: missing GVK constant and missing handler case\n\nEven if a developer manually added a `ResourceSlice` event string to `EventsToRegister()`:\n- `framework.ResourceSlice` does not exist as a constant in `types.go` \u2014 a raw string `\"ResourceSlice\"` would have to be used.\n- `addAllEventHandlers()`'s `switch gvk` has no `case framework.ResourceSlice:` arm. The `default` arm uses the dynamic informer factory but requires the GVK string to contain at least 2 dots (format: `<plural-kind>.<version>.<group>`). The string `\"ResourceSlice\"` has zero dots and would hit the `strings.Count(string(gvk), \".\") < 2` guard and be silently skipped via `continue`.\n\nThis means the full fix requires all three code changes described above to close the loop:\n1. Define the GVK constant.\n2. Register the event in the plugin.\n3. Wire the typed informer in `addAllEventHandlers()`.\n",

The plugin returns `Unschedulable` for all nodes, producing a `FitError`.\n   140\t\n   141\t### Step 4 \u2014 Pod lands in the unschedulable queue\n   142\t\n   143\tBack in `schedulingCycle()` (`schedule_one.go` line 159\u2013189), the `FitError` causes an `Unschedulable` status to be returned. `ScheduleOne()` at line 112\u2013114 calls `sched.FailureHandler()` \u2192 `handleSchedulingFailure()`, which enqueues the pod into the **unschedulable pod pool** of `SchedulingQueue`, labelled with `DynamicResources` as the rejecting plugin.\n   144\t\n   145\t### Step 5 \u2014 The scheduling queue's re-evaluation mechanism\n   146\t\n   147\tThe scheduling queue moves pods from the unschedulable pool to `activeQ` or `backoffQ` only when a matching **cluster event** fires. The mapping from \"which event re-queues which pod\" is maintained in `queueingHintsPerProfile`, built in `scheduler.go:buildQueueingHintMap()` by iterating over each plugin's `EventsToRegister()` list (lines 374\u2013410).\n   148\t\n   149\tFor a pod rejected by `DynamicResources`, the queue will call `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` only for cluster events that `DynamicResources` registered.\n   150\t\n   151\t### Step 6 \u2014 ResourceSlice events are not registered\n   152\t\n   153\t`dynamicResources.EventsToRegister()` (lines 386\u2013411) registers for:\n   154\t- `ResourceClaimParameters` Add/Update\n   155\t- `ResourceClassParameters` Add/Update\n   156\t- `ResourceClaim` Add/Update\n   157\t- `PodSchedulingContext` Add/Update\n   158\t- `Node` Add/UpdateNodeLabel/UpdateNodeTaint\n   159\t- `ResourceClass` Add/Update\n   160\t\n   161\t**`ResourceSlice` is conspicuously absent.**\n   162\t\n   163\tWhen the DRA driver starts and creates `ResourceSlice` objects, the `ResourceSlice` informer fires, but because `ResourceSlice` is not in `EventsToRegister()`, it is not in `gvkMap`, so `addAllEventHandlers()` never registers a callback for it. No `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` call is ever made for a `ResourceSlice` event.\n   164\t\n   165\t### Step 7 \u2014 Double absence: missing GVK constant and missing handler case\n   166\t\n   167\tEven if a developer manually added a `ResourceSlice` event string to `EventsToRegister()`:\n   168\t- `framework.ResourceSlice` does not exist as a constant in `types.go` \u2014 a raw string `\"ResourceSlice\"` would have to be used.\n   169\t- `addAllEventHandlers()`'s `switch gvk` has no `case framework.ResourceSlice:` arm. The `default` arm uses the dynamic informer factory but requires the GVK string to contain at least 2 dots (format: `<plural-kind>.<version>.<group>`). The string `\"ResourceSlice\"` has zero dots and would hit the `strings.Count(string(gvk), \".\") < 2` guard and be silently skipped via `continue`.\n   170\t\n   171\tThis means the full fix requires all three code changes described above to close the loop:\n   172\t1. Define the GVK constant.\n   173\t2. Register the event in the plugin.\n   174\t3. Wire the typed informer in `addAllEventHandlers()`.\n   175\t\n"

The scheduler never re-evaluates those pods.\n\n### Root Cause \u2014 Three coordinated defects\n\n**Primary defect** \u2014 `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go`, `EventsToRegister()` (lines ~386\u2013411):  \nThe plugin never registers a `ResourceSlice` Add/Update cluster event. The scheduler's re-queuing mechanism (`buildQueueingHintMap` \u2192 `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue`) can only wake a stuck pod when a cluster event matching its rejecting plugin's registered events fires. Because `ResourceSlice` is not in that list, no wake-up ever happens.\n\n**Supporting defect 1** \u2014 `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go`:  \nNo `ResourceSlice GVK = \"ResourceSlice\"` constant is defined. Without it, neither the plugin nor the event handler can reference the type canonically.\n\n**Supporting defect 2** \u2014 `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go`, `addAllEventHandlers()` switch:  \nNo `case framework.ResourceSlice:` arm exists to wire the typed informer. The `default` arm requires the GVK string to contain \u22652 dots (dynamic informer format); `\"ResourceSlice\"` has zero dots and is silently skipped via `continue`.\n\n### How the pod gets stuck (causal chain)\n\n1. `ScheduleOne()` \u2192 `schedulingCycle()` \u2192 `SchedulePod()` runs Filter plugins  \n2. `DynamicResources.PreFilter()` calls `newResourceModel()` \u2192 `resourceSliceLister.List()` \u2192 **zero results** (driver not started) \u2192 empty resource model  \n3. `DynamicResources.Filter()` calls `nodeIsSuitable(node, emptyResources)` \u2192 returns `false` for every node \u2192 `Unschedulable`  \n4. `handleSchedulingFailure()` places the pod in the **unschedulable pod pool**, tagged with `DynamicResources` as the rejecting plugin  \n5. Driver starts, creates `ResourceSlice` objects \u2014 informer fires, but no handler is registered \u2192 `MoveAllToActiveOrBackoffQueue()` is never called \u2192 **pod stuck forever**\n\n### Three-part fix\n\n| File | Change |\n|---|---|\n| `pkg/scheduler/framework/types.go` | Add `ResourceSlice GVK = \"ResourceSlice\"` |\n| `pkg/scheduler/framework/plugins/dynamicresources/dynamicresources.go` | Add `{Event: framework.ClusterEvent{Resource: framework.ResourceSlice, ActionType: framework.Add \\| framework.Update}}` to `EventsToRegister()` |\n| `pkg/scheduler/eventhandlers.go` | Add `case framework.ResourceSlice:` arm wiring `informerFactory.Resource().V1alpha2().ResourceSlices().Informer()` |"
